an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\\n39: \\n40: * lifecycle: \\n42: * backend: Fix nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\\n43: \\n44: * stacks: send progress events if the plan fails for better UI integration ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\\n45: \\n46: * cloud: terraform cloud and registry discovery This solves a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans  ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\\n49: \\n50: \\n51: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n52: \\n53: * backend/s3: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\\n54: \\n55: \\n56: EXPERIMENTS:\\n57: \\n58: Experiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\\n59: \\n60: - The experimental \\\"deferred actions\\\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\\n61: - `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\\n62: - `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\\n63:   - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\\n64:   - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\\n65: \\n66: ## Previous Releases\\n67: \\n68: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\\n69: \\n70: - This will produce warnings when passing in a value for a deprecated variable or when referencing a deprecated output. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\\n9: \\n10: * backend/s3: Support authentication via `aws login` ([#37967](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37967))\\n11: \\n12: \\n13: ENHANCEMENTS:\\n14: \\n15: * ssh-based provisioner (file + remote-exec): Re-enable support for PowerShell ([#37794](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37794))\\n16: \\n17: * terraform init log timestamps include millisecond precision ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\\n18: \\n19: * init: skip dependencies declared in development override. This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides and install dependencies that are not declared in the override file. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\\n20: \\n21: * Terraform Test: Allow functions within mock blocks ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\\n22: error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML skipped test elements, ensuring CI/CD pipelines can detect validation failures ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\\n29: \\n30: * A refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code with no changes ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\\n31: \\n32: * cli: Fixed crash in `terraform show -json` when plan contains ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\\n33: \\n34: * cli: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of plain text ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\\n35: \\n36: * `state show`: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail and return code 1 when it fails to render the named resources state ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\\n37: \\n38: * apply: Terraform will raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\\n39: \\n40: * lifecycle: `replace_triggered_by` now reports an error when given an invalid attribute reference that does not exist in the target resource ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\\n41: \\n42: * backend: Fix nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\\n43: \\n44: * stacks: send progress events if the plan fails for better UI integration ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\\n45: \\n46: * cloud: terraform cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, making temporary network or service related errors less common ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\\n47: \\n48: * stacks: component instances should report no-op plan/apply. This solves a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans  ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\\n49: \\n50: \\n51: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n52: \\n53: * backend/s3: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\\n54: \\n55: \\n56: EXPERIMENTS:\\n57: \\n58: Experiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\\n59: \\n60: - The experimental \\\"deferred actions\\\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\\n61: - `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\\n62: - `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\\n63:   - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. This allows test authors to keep long-running test infrastructure alive between test operations, saving time during regular test operations.\\n64:   - Test authors can now specify `skip_cleanup` attributes within test files and within run blocks. The `skip_cleanup` attribute tells `terraform test` not to clean up state files produced by run blocks with this attribute set to true. The state files for affected run blocks will be written to disk within the `.terraform` directory, where they can then be cleaned up manually using the also experimental `terraform test cleanup` command.\\n65: \\n66: ## Previous Releases\\n67: \\n68: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\\n69: \\n70: - This solves a UI inconsistency with convergence destroy plans  ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\\n49: \\n50: \\n51: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n52: \\n53: * backend/s3: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go. This replaces the previous behavior which treated any non-empty value as `true`. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\\n54: \\n55: \\n56: EXPERIMENTS:\\n57: \\n58: Experiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following features are not yet available in stable releases.\\n59: \\n60: - The experimental \\\"deferred actions\\\" feature, enabled by passing the `-allow-deferral` option to `terraform plan`, permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values and allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values.\\n61: - `terraform test cleanup`: The experimental `test cleanup` command. In experimental builds of Terraform, a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation during test operations are saved within the `.terraform` local directory. The `test cleanup` command will attempt to clean up the local state files left behind automatically, without requiring manual intervention.\\n62: - `terraform test`: `backend` blocks and `skip_cleanup` attributes:\\n63:   - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks in Terraform Test files. Run blocks with `backend` blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting from empty state on every execution. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01CXCaQKP8wJkm4R3RF3e7o5","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01CwKgF42f2S7UEvwFngAP74","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/CHANGELOG.md","content":"## Terraform v1.15.0 (Unreleased)\n\n### Breaking Changes\n\n- **backend/s3**: The `AWS_USE_FIPS_ENDPOINT` and `AWS_USE_DUALSTACK_ENDPOINT` environment variables now only respect `true` or `false` values, aligning with the AWS SDK for Go v2. Previously, any non-empty value was treated as `true`. Update your environment variable exports to use explicit `true` or `false` values instead of relying on implicit truthy behavior. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n### New Features\n\n- **command/validate**: The `validate` command now checks the `backend` block for errors. This ensures the backend type exists, that all required attributes are present, and that the backend's own validation logic passes. This allows validation failures in backend configuration to be detected earlier without running `terraform init`. ([#38021](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38021))\n\n- **core/variables**: You can now set a `deprecated` attribute on `variable` and `output` blocks to indicate that they are deprecated. Terraform will produce warnings when a value is passed to a deprecated variable or when a deprecated output is referenced. This allows module authors to guide users toward using newer input/output names. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n- **backend/s3**: The S3 backend now supports authentication via AWS SSO using `aws login`. This enables users to leverage their AWS CLI SSO configuration directly within Terraform without manually managing long-lived credentials. ([#37967](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37967))\n\n- **build**: Terraform now produces official builds for Windows ARM64 (`terraform_windows_arm64`), enabling support for ARM-based Windows environments. ([#32719](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/32719))\n\n### Enhancements\n\n- **provisioner/remote-exec**: SSH-based provisioners (file and remote-exec) now re-enable support for PowerShell on Windows systems. This restores the ability to use PowerShell scripts within remote-exec provisioners on Windows targets. ([#37794](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37794))\n\n- **command/init**: The `terraform init` command now includes millisecond precision in log timestamps, improving the ability to correlate logs with other systems that use millisecond precision. ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\n\n- **command/init**: The `terraform init` command now skips dependencies declared in development overrides. This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides and install dependencies that are not declared in the override file, enabling more flexible local development workflows. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n\n- **moduletest**: Terraform Test now allows function calls within mock blocks. Previously, mock blocks only supported literal values; they can now use built-in functions to construct more complex mock data. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n- **lang/deprecated**: Detection of deprecated resource attributes and blocks has been improved, providing more accurate warnings to users when they use deprecated schema elements. ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n- **moduletest/junit**: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML output for skipped test elements. This ensures CI/CD pipelines can properly detect and report validation failures that occur during Terraform test operations. ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n\n- **command/refresh**: Fixed an issue where a refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code despite having no changes to report. The exit code now correctly reflects whether changes were detected. ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n\n- **command/show**: Fixed a crash in `terraform show -json` that occurred when a plan contained ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON serialization now handles these special resource types correctly. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n- **command/init**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing plain text and JSON. All output is now consistently formatted as JSON when `-json` is specified. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n- **command/state**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with exit code 1 when it cannot render the state for named resources. This provides clearer feedback when the command encounters issues, rather than potentially succeeding with partial output. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n- **command/apply**: Terraform will now raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace. This prevents accidental application of plans to the wrong workspace, which could lead to unintended infrastructure changes. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n- **core/lifecycle**: The `replace_triggered_by` meta-argument now validates attribute references and reports an error when given an invalid reference that does not exist in the target resource. This prevents silent failures and provides clearer error messages during plan. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n- **backend**: Fixed a nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error. The initialization process now handles backend errors gracefully without panicking. ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n- **stacks**: Fixed an issue where stacks did not send progress events when a plan failed. This improves UI integration for Terraform stacks by ensuring complete event reporting even in error scenarios. ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n\n- **cloud**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, with improved error handling for temporary network or service-related failures. This reduces the frequency of transient errors during operations that depend on cloud connectivity. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n\n- **stacks**: Fixed a UI inconsistency where component instances in convergence destroy plans were not reporting no-op plan/apply operations correctly. Component instances now properly report when no changes are needed. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n### Experiments\n\nExperiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. The following experimental features are not yet available in stable releases:\n\n- **Deferred Actions** (`-allow-deferral`): This experimental feature permits `count` and `for_each` arguments in `module`, `resource`, and `data` blocks to have unknown values. It allows providers to react more flexibly to unknown values by deferring operations that cannot proceed without complete information.\n\n- **Terraform Test Cleanup** (`terraform test cleanup`): In experimental builds, when test operations fail, Terraform saves a manifest file and state files for each failed cleanup operation in the `.terraform` local directory. The experimental `test cleanup` command attempts to clean up these local state files automatically without requiring manual intervention.\n\n- **Terraform Test Backend Blocks and Skip Cleanup**:\n  - Test authors can now specify `backend` blocks within `run` blocks. Run blocks with backend blocks will load state from the specified backend instead of starting with empty state, allowing test infrastructure to remain active between test operations.\n  - Test authors can specify `skip_cleanup` attributes in test files and run blocks. State files for affected run blocks are written to disk in the `.terraform` directory and can be cleaned up manually using the experimental `test cleanup` command.\n\n### Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- Previously, any non-empty value was treated as `true`. Update your environment variable exports to use explicit `true` or `false` values instead of relying on implicit truthy behavior. ([#37601](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37601))\n\n### New Features\n\n- **command/validate**: The `validate` command now checks the `backend` block for errors. This ensures the backend type exists, that all required attributes are present, and that the backend's own validation logic passes. This allows validation failures in backend configuration to be detected earlier without running `terraform init`. ([#38021](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38021))\n\n- **core/variables**: You can now set a `deprecated` attribute on `variable` and `output` blocks to indicate that they are deprecated. Terraform will produce warnings when a value is passed to a deprecated variable or when a deprecated output is referenced. This allows module authors to guide users toward using newer input/output names. ([#38001](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38001))\n\n- **backend/s3**: The S3 backend now supports authentication via AWS SSO using `aws login`. This enables users to leverage their AWS CLI SSO configuration directly within Terraform without manually managing long-lived credentials. ([#37967](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37967))\n\n- **build**: Terraform now produces official builds for Windows ARM64 (`terraform_windows_arm64`), enabling support for ARM-based Windows environments. ([#32719](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/32719))\n\n### Enhancements\n\n- **provisioner/remote-exec**: SSH-based provisioners (file and remote-exec) now re-enable support for PowerShell on Windows systems. This restores the ability to use PowerShell scripts within remote-exec provisioners on Windows targets. ([#37794](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37794))\n\n- **command/init**: The `terraform init` command now includes millisecond precision in log timestamps, improving the ability to correlate logs with other systems that use millisecond precision. ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\n\n- **command/init**: The `terraform init` command now skips dependencies declared in development overrides. This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides and install dependencies that are not declared in the override file, enabling more flexible local development workflows. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n\n- **moduletest**: Terraform Test now allows function calls within mock blocks. Previously, mock blocks only supported literal values; they can now use built-in functions to construct more complex mock data. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n- **lang/deprecated**: Detection of deprecated resource attributes and blocks has been improved, providing more accurate warnings to users when they use deprecated schema elements. ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n- **moduletest/junit**: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML output for skipped test elements. This ensures CI/CD pipelines can properly detect and report validation failures that occur during Terraform test operations. ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n\n- **command/refresh**: Fixed an issue where a refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code despite having no changes to report. The exit code now correctly reflects whether changes were detected. ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n\n- **command/show**: Fixed a crash in `terraform show -json` that occurred when a plan contained ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON serialization now handles these special resource types correctly. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n- **command/init**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing plain text and JSON. All output is now consistently formatted as JSON when `-json` is specified. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n- **command/state**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with exit code 1 when it cannot render the state for named resources. This provides clearer feedback when the command encounters issues, rather than potentially succeeding with partial output. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n- **command/apply**: Terraform will now raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace. This prevents accidental application of plans to the wrong workspace, which could lead to unintended infrastructure changes. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n- **core/lifecycle**: The `replace_triggered_by` meta-argument now validates attribute references and reports an error when given an invalid reference that does not exist in the target resource. This prevents silent failures and provides clearer error messages during plan. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n- **backend**: Fixed a nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error. The initialization process now handles backend errors gracefully without panicking. ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n- **stacks**: Fixed an issue where stacks did not send progress events when a plan failed. This improves UI integration for Terraform stacks by ensuring complete event reporting even in error scenarios. ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n\n- **cloud**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, with improved error handling for temporary network or service-related failures. This reduces the frequency of transient errors during operations that depend on cloud connectivity. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n\n- **stacks**: Fixed a UI inconsistency where component instances in convergence destroy plans were not reporting no-op plan/apply operations correctly. Component instances now properly report when no changes are needed. ([#38049](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38049))\n\n### Experiments\n\nExperiments are only enabled in alpha releases of Terraform CLI. ([#37818](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37818))\n\n- **command/init**: The `terraform init` command now skips dependencies declared in development overrides. This allows you to use `terraform init` with developer overrides and install dependencies that are not declared in the override file, enabling more flexible local development workflows. ([#37884](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37884))\n\n- **moduletest**: Terraform Test now allows function calls within mock blocks. Previously, mock blocks only supported literal values; they can now use built-in functions to construct more complex mock data. ([#34672](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/34672))\n\n- **lang/deprecated**: Detection of deprecated resource attributes and blocks has been improved, providing more accurate warnings to users when they use deprecated schema elements. ([#38077](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38077))\n\n### Bug Fixes\n\n- **moduletest/junit**: File-level error diagnostics are now included in JUnit XML output for skipped test elements. This ensures CI/CD pipelines can properly detect and report validation failures that occur during Terraform test operations. ([#37801](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37801))\n\n- **command/refresh**: Fixed an issue where a refresh-only plan could result in a non-zero exit code despite having no changes to report. The exit code now correctly reflects whether changes were detected. ([#37406](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37406))\n\n- **command/show**: Fixed a crash in `terraform show -json` that occurred when a plan contained ephemeral resources with preconditions or postconditions. The JSON serialization now handles these special resource types correctly. ([#37834](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37834))\n\n- **command/init**: Fixed `terraform init -json` to properly format all backend configuration messages as JSON instead of mixing plain text and JSON. All output is now consistently formatted as JSON when `-json` is specified. ([#37911](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37911))\n\n- **command/state**: The `state show` command will now explicitly fail with exit code 1 when it cannot render the state for named resources. This provides clearer feedback when the command encounters issues, rather than potentially succeeding with partial output. ([#37933](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37933))\n\n- **command/apply**: Terraform will now raise an explicit error if a plan file intended for one workspace is applied against another workspace. This prevents accidental application of plans to the wrong workspace, which could lead to unintended infrastructure changes. ([#37954](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/37954))\n\n- **core/lifecycle**: The `replace_triggered_by` meta-argument now validates attribute references and reports an error when given an invalid reference that does not exist in the target resource. This prevents silent failures and provides clearer error messages during plan. ([#36740](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36740))\n\n- **backend**: Fixed a nil pointer dereference crash during `terraform init` when the destination backend returns an error. The initialization process now handles backend errors gracefully without panicking. ([#38027](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38027))\n\n- **stacks**: Fixed an issue where stacks did not send progress events when a plan failed. This improves UI integration for Terraform stacks by ensuring complete event reporting even in error scenarios. ([#38039](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38039))\n\n- **cloud**: Terraform Cloud and registry discovery network requests are now more resilient, with improved error handling for temporary network or service-related failures. This reduces the frequency of transient errors during operations that depend on cloud connectivity. ([#38064](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/38064))\n","numLines":50,"startLine":1,"totalLines":89}}}
